## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population growth dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time derivative of population size P, indicating an underlying population growth ODE model in ecology. Typical relationships express growth as per-capita rate functions of P (density dependence) and/or explicit time dependence (environmental forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (environmental trend in growth rate)
- Seasonally forced exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment)
- Logistic growth ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear density dependence with carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Logistic with constant harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (external removal independent of P)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (harvest/predation saturates at high P)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (nonlinear crowding with shape exponent c2)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (per-capita growth decreases ~ log(P))
- Richards growth ODE (generalized logistic family): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoid via exponent c2)
- Allee effect (weak/strong depensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P, carrying-capacity limit at high P)
- Polynomial crowding (multi-equilibria): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order density dependence)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (non-autonomous logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t + c3 * sin(c4 * t))) (K changes with trend/seasonality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If (dP_dt) / P is approximately constant over P and t, the structure dP_dt = c0 * P (exponential growth/decay) is indicated.
- If (dP_dt) / P decreases roughly linearly with P, use logistic-type terms P*(1 - c*P) implying a single stable carrying capacity.
- If (dP_dt) / P decreases roughly with log(P), a Gompertz form P*log(c/(P+c)) often fits (rapid early growth, long tail to asymptote).
- If growth is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P, include an Allee factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying P (depensation/critical threshold).
- If the approach to carrying capacity is sharper or flatter than logistic, include a shape exponent on P inside the density-dependence term (theta-logistic/Richards).
- If dP_dt shows periodic fluctuations at fixed P, include explicit sinusoidal forcing in coefficients (seasonal environment).
- If dP_dt remains bounded as P grows but removal appears to saturate, add rational loss terms like P/(P+c) (saturating harvest/predation).
- If multiple nonzero equilibria appear (growth crosses zero more than once for P>0), use higher-order polynomials in P or products of linear factors in P.

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 52

GT (fixed):  
\[
0.5980421691\,(1-\tfrac{P}{32.9394024023})P\;+\;0.5980421691\,(1-e^{-0.07682777496P})P
\]
Expand structure:
\[
= \underbrace{0.5980421691P}_{\text{linear}}-\underbrace{\frac{0.5980421691}{32.9394}P^2}_{\text{quadratic}}+\underbrace{0.5980421691P}_{\text{linear}}-\underbrace{0.5980421691\,P e^{-0.07682777496P}}_{\text{P*exp(neg*P)}}
\]
So GT is exactly of the form:
\[
A\,P^2 + B\,P + D\,P\,e^{kP}
\]
with \(A\neq 0\), \(B\neq 0\), and \(D\neq 0\) and \(k=-0.07682777496\). Also **no constant term**, and **no dependence on \(t\)**.

Now check candidates for whether they can be reduced (by choosing constants) to exactly \(A P^2 + B P + D P e^{kP}\) with no extra terms.

1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + Pc4 + P^{c5}c6e^{Pc7} + c8\): has extra \(P^{c5}e^{Pc7}\) term unless \(c6=0\). Also has extra \(Pc4\) and constant \(c8\) but those can be set to 0 or absorbed into \(Pc1\). After setting \(c6=0, c8=0\), it becomes \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c4) + P c2 e^{Pc3}\), which matches GT form. **Match possible.**

2. Same as (1) but with extra \(Pc5\), constant \(c6\), and log term. Set log coefficient \(c7=0\), set \(c6=0\), absorb \(Pc5\) into \(Pc1/Pc4\). Reduces to \(P^2c0 + P(\cdot) + Pc2e^{Pc3}\). **Match possible.**

3. Has \(P^{c2}\log(Pc4+1)\) and \(P^{c5}e^{Pc7}\). To match GT we must kill the log term (set \(c3=0\)) and make the exp term exactly \(P e^{kP}\) (set \(c5=1\)). Then expression is \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c6 e^{Pc7} + c8\). Set \(c8=0\). **Match possible.**

4. Contains \(P^3\) and multiple \(P^2\) terms and many linear terms plus \(P e^{Pc7}\). Set \(c0=0\) to remove \(P^3\). Combine \(P^2\) coefficients into one (choose \(c1,c2,c3\) to sum to desired \(A\)). Combine linear terms \(Pc4,Pc5,Pc8\) into desired \(B\). Set constant \(c9=0\). Keep \(P c6 e^{Pc7}\) for the exponential term. **Match possible.**

5. Has extra power term \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) which is generally \(P^{c4+1}\). To avoid unwanted powers, set \(c2=0\) (kill it). Then it’s \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c5 e^{Pc6} + P(c7+c8)+c9\). Set \(c9=0\), absorb linear terms. **Match possible.**

6. Like (1) but extra \(P^{c6}c7e^{Pc8}\). Set \(c7=0\) to remove it; set \(c9=0\). Remaining \(P^2c0 + P(\cdot) + Pc2e^{Pc3}\). **Match possible.**

7. \(P^2c0 + P*P^{c1}c2 + Pc3 + Pc4e^{Pc5} + Pc6+Pc7+Pc8+c9\). Need no extra nonlinear power term: set \(c2=0\) (or set \(c1=0\) gives linear \(Pc2\), but easiest kill). Then combine linear terms into \(B\), set constant \(c9=0\), keep \(Pc4e^{Pc5}\). **Match possible.**

8. Same logic as (7) (no constant term here except \(c8\) which is constant): set \(c2=0\), set \(c8=0\), combine linear terms, keep \(Pc4e^{Pc5}\). **Match possible.**

9. Has rational term \(c7/(P^2c8+1)\) which GT doesn’t have; must set \(c7=0\). Also set constant \(c6=0\). Then reduces to \(P^2c0 + P(\cdot) + Pc2e^{Pc3}\). **Match possible.**

10. Has \(P^3\) (kill with \(c0=0\)), has \(c6 e^{Pc7}\) and \(c8 e^{Pc9}\) (pure exponentials without \(P\) factor). GT needs \(P e^{kP}\), not \(e^{kP}\). You cannot turn \(e^{kP}\) into \(P e^{kP}\) by constants. Only option is to set those exponential terms to 0, but then you lose the required \(P e^{kP}\) term. **No match.**

11. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2e^{Pc3} + c4 + c5e^{Pc6} + c7e^{Pc8}\). Any \(e^{Pc6}\) terms are missing the required prefactor \(P\). You could set \(c5=c7=0\), but then you’d need \(P^2\) term and linear+quadratic; you only have \(Pc0\) and possibly \(P^{c1}e^{Pc3}\). If set \(c1=1\), you get \(P e^{Pc3}\) (good), but still no \(P^2\) term. If set \(c1=2\), you get \(P^2 e^{Pc3}\) (wrong). **No match.**

12. Has \(c7/(c8|P|+1)\) non-analytic absolute value; must set \(c7=0\). Then it’s \(P^2c0 + P(\cdot) + Pc2e^{Pc3} + c6\). Set \(c6=0\). **Match possible.**

13. Has \(P c6 \log(c7|P+c8|+1)\) which cannot equal a polynomial+ \(P e^{kP}\) for all \(P\) unless coefficient is 0. Set \(c6=0\), set constant \(c9=0\). Remaining matches form. **Match possible.**

14. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + Pc3 + P c4 e^{Pc5} + Pc6 + c7 + c8 e^{Pc5}\). The \(c8 e^{Pc5}\) term is pure exponential (no \(P\)); must set \(c8=0\). Kill \(P^3\) with \(c0=0\). Set constant \(c7=0\). Then \(P^2c1 + P(\cdot) + P c4 e^{Pc5}\). **Match possible.**

15. Has \(P c5 \log(c6/(P+c7)+1)\) which cannot appear in GT; set \(c5=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + P(\cdot) + c8\); but then no \(P e^{kP}\) term. **No match.**

16. Has \(P c5/(P+c6)\) rational; must set \(c5=0\). Then no exponential term. **No match.**

But still missing a \(P^2\) term unless you can create it elsewhere (you can’t). So unless you keep \(P*P^{c0}c1\) as \(P^2\) by setting \(c0=1\), giving \(c1 P^2\). That works: choose \(c0=1\) to make \(P^2\) term, keep \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\), combine linear terms \(Pc2+Pc5\), set constant \(c6=0\). **Match possible.**

This lacks the separate linear term? Actually it has \(Pc1\) yes, and exponential term \(P c2 e^{Pc3}\) yes. GT also has linear+quadratic+that exponential term, so OK. **Match possible.**
